\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_000_metadata
\ref Recorded on 01 April 2010 in Yakutsk by Natalia Aralova and Brigitte Pakendorf, in the speaker's office at the
Department of Northern Philology at the Faculty of Philology, Yakutsk State University, in the afternoon. The office was
a small room with windows facing the street. At the recording, only NA and BP were present. It was relatively quiet,
though EAK occasionally knocked against a stool with her foot, and some traffic noises are audible. 
\qu Transcribed in pen and paper by XXX??? (Ekaterina Afanasevna??), and transcribed in Elan by Katharina Gernet. Translated into
Russian by Ekaterina Afanas'evna Krivoshapkina, glossed by BP. Funding by the Volkswagen Foundation (DoBeS grant). Speaker
abbreviation = EAK.
\ref Ekaterina Afanas'evna Krivoshapkina was 39 years old at the time of recording. She has a diploma in Even philology and
works as a lecturer at the Department of Northern Philology. She spends every summer in the reindeer herd with her
parents, her brother, and her son. She is the daughter of Afanasij Vasilevich Krivoshapkin (from stado 9) and Anastasija
Afanas'evna Kejmetinova.

\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_005
\ref
\tx Stadala        bi   ammụ           gurgewčin,       ujis        stadala,       tiekte    gurgewčin        nọŋan,
\mb stado  -(dU)LE biː aman   -W        gurgeːwči -n(I) ujun -Is    stado  -(dU)LE tiek =DE  gurgeːwči -n(I) nọŋan
\ge herd.R -loc    1sg  father -poss.1sg work        -3sg  nine -ord.Y herd.R -loc    now  =ptl work        -3sg  3sg

\tx adịːda    anŋanị, digen mịardụk        hulčedʒin,                         tala          nọŋan
\mb adịː =DE  anŋan     digen mịan -L  -DUk(U) hul              -čE    -DʒI -n(I) tarak -(dU)LE nọŋan
\ge some    =ptl year       four  ten    -pl -abl    remain.in.excess -pf.ptc -fut -3sg   dist  -loc    3sg

\tx gurgewčideŋen.
\mb gurgeːwči -DEŋ    -E-n(I)
\ge work        -pst.ptc -ep-poss.3sg
\ft In the herd my father works, in the 9th brigade, he works there now, many years, it's probably more than 40 years that he has worked in the
herd.
\ph
\gr checked with Ekaterina Afanasevna, 19.03.13, anŋanị = Sebjan version of anŋan; adịːda anŋanị = uzhe mnogo let; anŋannị  or anŋanụ = NO
--> biː anŋanịŋụ = moj vozrast, moi gody, nọŋan anŋanịŋan
\ph
\comment
\ru В стаде работает мой отец, в 9-ом стаде, и сейчас он работает; много  лет, наверно, более 40 там он работает.
\ev Стадала би амму гургэвчин, уйис? стадала, тиэктэ гургэвчин ноӈан;  ади-да анӈини, дигэнмиардук hулчэдьин, тала ноӈан гургэвчидэӈэн.

\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_006
\ref
\tx Nọŋan Afanasij Vasilevič Krivošapkin gee... gerbe.
\mb nọŋan Afanasij Vasilevič Krivošapkin gerbe  gerbe
\ge 3sg      Afanasij Vasilevich Krivoshapkin name   name
\ft He is called Afanasij Vasilevich Krivoshapkin.
\ph
\gr here, gerbe is like Sakha 'dien', it is literally "on po imeni AVK", not 'his name is'; one can also say gerbelken, but just gerbe is more common
\ph
\comment
\ru Эго зовут Афанасий Васильевич Кривошапкин.
\ev Ноӈан Афанасий Васильевич Кривошапкин гэр... гэрбэ.

\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_012
\ref
\tx Tiemi     mut    ọranat                   ịadụk,    bileːktuk        Sebeːnduk            ọranat
\mb teːmi    mut    ọrọn          -E  -Č  ịak -DUk(U) bileːk   -DUk(U) Sebjan-Küöl -DUk(U) ọrọn          -E -Č
\ge therefore 1pl.in domestic.reindeer -ep -ins what  -abl    territory -abl    Sebjan-Küöl -abl    domestic.reindeer -ep -ins

\tx gu... gulehŋererep.
\mb gu    gulehen              -Gr(E) -R(E) -p
\ge Q     ride.off.by.reindeer -hab   -nonfut -1pl.in

\ft Therefor we went out from the village, from Sebjan by reindeer.
\ph
\gr gulehendej = lamunkhinskij word, vyezhatj, otkochevyvatj imenno na olenjax, synonym of nulgehendej, but with focus on VYezzhaem,
doesn't exist without the limitative suffix, i.e. guledej = NO; but one can say gulehnep "vyexali, poexali"
\comment
\ru Поэтому мы на оленях делали... из Себяна на оленях выезжали.
\ev Тиэми мут оранат иарит (иаду?) ... билэктук Себэндук оранат гу ...  гулэhӈэрэрэп.

\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_017
\ref
\tx Ŋiː, Toŋekčen gerbe torre.
\mb ŋiː  Toŋekčen gerbe tor   -(dU)LE
\ge who    Tongekchen name  earth -loc
\ft It's in a place called Tongekchen.
\ph
\gr Toŋekčen is derived from toŋke, "patch forest with big tall trees", in that place there used to be a wood like that, but now it has been largely cut
down for wood
\comment
\ru Это... В местность под названием Төӈэкчэн.
\ev Ни ... Төӈэкчэн гэрбэ төррэ.

\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_018
\ref
\tx Tar   Toŋekčendule     ịhrakat,                       ịaka, atịkal,     etikel,      ọralčịmŋal
\mb tarak Toŋekčen -(dU)LE ịs  -REk      -E  -t(I)        ịak   atịkan  -L  etikeːn -L  ọrọlčị -mŋE -L
\ge dist  Tongekchen -loc    reach -cond.cvb -ep -poss.1pl.in what    old.woman -pl old.man  -pl herd.reindeer -agnr -pl

\tx oreldewrer           delbi, ńan   muttuk         honte, ejmu             noːn                     Tamara Afanasevna
\mb orelde   -Gr(E) -r   delbi  ńaːn mut    -DUk(U) honte  enen   -W        noː            -n(I)     Tamara Afanasevna
\ge be.happy -hab   -3pl very.Y and    1pl.in -abl    other  mother -poss.1sg younger.sibling -poss.3sg Tamara Afanasevna

\tx kụŋalčal      ńan   muttule        ujis        stadala        ńoːwrerin                 deremketnemi.
\mb kụŋa -L  -čEl ńaːn mut    -(dU)LE ujun -Is    stado  -(dU)LE ńoː -Gr(E) -RI -n(I)      deremke -Č  -nE     -mI
\ge child   -pl -com  and    1pl.in -loc    nine -ord.Y herd.R -loc    exit  -hab   -pst -poss.3sg rest    -res -intent -cond.cvb
\ft When we reached that Tongekchen, the old women and men, the reindeer herders were very happy, and apart from us my mother's younger
sister Tamara Afanasevna also went to us, to the 9th brigade, with her children to rest.
\ph
\gr 19.03.13, questions2, 10:15, deremketnemi from deremkettej, deremkenemi - she hadn't heard this form, it's usually deremketnemi, but there is
a word biː deremkerem is OK, while deremkettem = perhaps more literary;  Tamara Afanasevna kụŋalčal ńoːwrerin - she is the main argument,
the others just with her; it would also be OK to say T.A. kụŋalčal ńoːwreritnen
\comment
\ru Когда мы туда доезжали, это старухи-старики, оленеводы радуются очень  и кроме нас, младшая сестра матери Тамара Афанасьевна с
детьми тоже к  нам в 9-ое стадо выезжала отдыхать.
\ev Тар Төӈэкчэндулэ иhракат иака амикал - этикэл, этикэл, оралчимӈал  өрэлдэврэр дэлби ниан муттун hөнтэ эйму нөн Тамара Афанасьевна 
куӈалчал ниан муттулэ уйус стадала ньөврэрин дэрэмкэтнэми.

\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_020
\ref
\tx Mut,   tar   omettu   baldačal           hurelten             họː họːja biwrep.

\gr (questions3_20032013, 7:00) ọːn kojeːčem = kak smotretj za olenjami, (the verb could be replaced by irgečem, irgettej = vospityvatj detej,
uxaxhivatj za zhivotnymi), ili ọŋkụčam = gde kormitj; ọːn kojeːttiwen = NO; biː ọŋkụčam = NO; ọŋkụča = NO, there is a verb ọŋkụttaj, ọrọn
ọŋkọddọn = sam kormitsja, bej ọrọm ọŋkụttan = chelovek kormit olenja; bej ọrọn ọŋkụča = NO;  then she said "ọŋkọčọn skoree ne glagol",
= kormlenie; ili ọŋkụčam = gde luchshee kormlenie; ọrọm ọːn kojeːttej = NO, --> oːn ọrọm kojeːčepti (this is a little bit similar to kojeːčem, but
not completely); ọːn ọrọm kojeːčeptij, ọːn ọŋkụčaptịw amandụkụj haːllịw (sounds like prfl. on first verb and acc on second - maybe she made a
mistake); ili horečem = NO --> ili horeptiw; ọːn gurgewčičem = NO --> ọːn gurgewčiptiw/ọːn gurgewčim = OK;  ọːn tegečem = OK, kak
zhitj; --> I'm not sure about the analysis of kojeːčem, ọŋkụčam, but it would seem to make the most sense, since it's clearly a noun, and clearly
an accusative, and clearly derived from resultative verbs
\gr (questions6_25032013, 0:45) can one say: amandụkụj ili horem haːllịw --> ili biwettij "gde bytj, gde ezditj" would be better or ili biwettiw haːllịw
(i.e. impersonal), or one could say ile biwečeptiw haːllịw; ile horem haːllịw - not so good, ile horeptiw haːllịw would be better; ọːn gurgewčim
amandụkụj haːllịw = seems OK, kakuju rabotu delatj; ọːn gurgewčiptiw haːllịw = kak rabotatj uznala; ọːn ọŋkụčọn = gde i kak proizvoditj
kormlenie --> so it seems as if my analysis of kojeːčem, ọŋkụčam are correct

\id Krivoshapkina_EA_reindeer_herd_198
\ref
\tx Tar   ụntačamị            tettidʒi,      bombodʒeːgegej                 gịrkawran,         hutu.
\mb tarak ụnta    -čEn -J       tet    -RIdʒI  bombon              -dʒEːgEgEj gịrka -Gr(E) -n(I) hut   -W
\ge dist  fur.boots -dim  -prfl.sg put.on -ant.cvb be.small.and.chubby -dim.tender  walk    -hab   -3sg  child -poss.1sg

\gr (questions4_22032013, 22:50) bombodʒeːgegej = xodil takoj malenkij i puxlyj, used for children, a similar form would be bụŋtadʒaːgagaj, then
she said bụŋtaŋakan, bụŋtaŋaja if big, tender words with respect to children
\gr (questions6_25032013, 3:30) bombodʒeːgegej kụŋa/l = OK, kụŋa bombodʒeːgegej gịrkawran = OK, rebenok puxlenko idet, perevalivaetsja;
gudʒedʒeːgegej = NO --> gudʒeńe, gudʒeńekie, gudʒeńekiekeken; kotledʒeːgegej = NO --> kotlekeken; hebdʒendʒeːgegej = NO;
pelpedʒeːgegej mozhno skazatj, e.g. pelpedʒeːgegej nekelleren = nachal xvastatsja, balovatsja, shumetj, otritsatelno, but at end said that this was
said with love, i.e. you see the bad side of your child but you still love it, whereas just pelpeŋeken lacks this meaning of tenderness; als found in
kịawadʒaːgagaj = krivo, ịaldadʒaːgagaj "chernenkij", dụrbadʒaːgagaj "belenkij"; dʒergedʒeːgegej (from dʒergen, become excited) = OK,
debedʒeːgegej (from deben, become shaggy) = OK; -dʒeːgegej = ljubja (though EAK analyses the suffix as only -gEgEj, so that I wonder
whether the -dʒEː part comes from the durative-diminutive) --> but overall it seems to derive adwords from descriptive verbs with a meaning of
tenderness
\gr on 26.03.2013 I checked without recording: bombogegej = NO, only bombodʒeːgegej; pelpegegej = NO, only pelpedʒeːgegej; dụrbagagaj =
NO, only dụrbadʒaːgagaj --> clearly the morpheme contains -dʒEː, even if it perhaps goes back to a frozen durative suffix; tutedʒeːgegej = NO
--> tutenedden; ewiːdʒeːgegej = NO (and she was quite clear about the unacceptability of these) --> it really seems to be a derivation of tender
diminutive adwords from descriptive verbs, not any kind of verb
\nt
\comment
\ru Надев эти свои унточки, переваливаясь ходил мой ребёнок.
\ev Тар унтачами тэттидьи, бөмбөдьэгэгэй гиркавран hуту.
